MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Mr. Steve Mallen, Laboratory Support Division
FROM: Suzanne Jones, QA/QC Chemist, MEC/STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report for week ending March 3, 1998
1. GB
* 12 hour QP chart shows zero points out of the control limits. The QPs continue to trend on the low
side of the average percent recovery, which indicates an out-of-control situation accordling to the
LQCP. However, this percent recovery value is based on data collected from the months of
November and December. Please give direction as to the acceptability of this current method for
updating recovery rates.
* 2 hour QP chart shows zero points out of the control limits. QPs also trending on the low side of
the average percent recovery.
0 Perimeter QP chart shows one point out of the control limits for the last seven days. The point was
investigated and an assignable cause has not been found.
* Igloo QP chart shows three points out of the control limits. The points were investigated and no
assignable cause has been found.
2. VX
* 12 hour QP chart shows two points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The two points
were investigated and no assignable cause has been found.
* 2 hour QP chart shows five points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The points were
investigated and no assignable cause has been found. Two points were not plotted due to
integration error. One point was not plotted due to operator error.
* Perimeter QP chart shows two points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The points
were investigated and no assignable cause was found.
0 Igloo QP chart shows two points out of the control limits. The points were investigated and no
assignable cause has been found.
3. HD
* 12 hour QP chart shows two points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The two points
were investigated and no assignable cause has been found.
* 2 hour QP chart shows zero points out of the control limits for the last seven days.
* Perimeter QP chart shows one point out of the control limits. The point was investigated and no
assignable cause was found. However, due to the improved recoveries of the QPs all points are on
the high side of the average percent recovery line indicating an out-of-control situation. Again, this
is due to the current method of updating control liinits(i.e. using data from 3-4 months ago.) Please
give direction as to the acceptability of this current method for updating recovery rates.
* Igloo QP chart shows zero points out of the control limits.
4. GA
* All QP scenarios continue to reflect poor recoveries. Investigations are ongoing to determine a
cause for these out of control situations but no explanations have been found.
* 12 hour QP chart shows six points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The points were
investigated and no assignable cause has been found.
* 2 hour QP chart shows five points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The points were
investigated and no assignable cause has been found.

Mellor Engineering Corporation/Science and Technology Corporation February 25, 1998
MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Mr. Steve Mallen, Chief, Laboratory Support Division
FROM: Steve Freudenberger, MEC/STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report for week of February 17-24, 1997
1. GB
a 12 hour QP chart shows zero points out of the control limits. However, the QPs continue to trend
on the low side of the target concentration. No explanations for this occurrence have been found.
* 2 hour chart shows zero points out of the control limits for the last seven days.
* Perimeter QP charts shows three points out of the control limits for the last seven days. The three
points were investigated and an assignable cause has not been found.
2. VX
* 12 hour QP chart has one point out of the control limits. The point was investigated and no
assignable cause has been found. Precision has improved over the last seven days.
* 2 hour QP chart shows four points outside the control limits. The four points were investigated
and no assignable cause was found. Three points were not plotted due to spiking error.
a Perimeter QP chart has one point out of control. The point was investigated and no assignable
cause was found.
3. HD
* 12 hour QP chart has one point out of the control limits. The point was investigated and no
assignable cause was found. Three points were not plotted due to spiking error.
* 2 hour QP chart has two points out of the control limits. The point was investigated and no
assignable cause was found.
0 Perimeter QP chart has zero points out of the control limits. The recovery rate has increased by
approximately 10% over the last two weeks.
4. GA
* All QP scenarios continue to reflect very poor recoveries. Investigations are ongoing to determine
a cause for these out of control situations but no explanations have been found. The requirements
(recovery of plus or minus 25%) set forth in the quality control plans are not being fulfilled.
Therefor, it is recommended, that analysis for GA on DAAMS tubes using our current method be
suspended until either a new method is adapted or the requirements (mentioned above)be changed
in the quality control plan.
POC for this is Steve Freudenberger, X449 1.
Steve Freudenberger
Chief, Analysis Branch
STC/MEC Team

SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report for week ending Deeewbz , 9,97
1. GB3
* 12 hour QP chart has seven points out of control with no assignable cause. QPs continue to trend
on the low side of the target concentration. No explanations for this occurrence have been found.
2 hour and Perimeter QP charts look good.
2. VX
* 12 hour QP chart has nine points out of control with no assignable cause. 2 hour QP chart has one
point out of control. Perimeter QP chart has 2 points out of control with no assignable cause.
3. HD
* 12 hour QP chart has three points out of control with no assignable cause. 2 hour QP chart has two
points out of control with no assignable cause. Perimeter QP chart has three points out of control
with no assignable cause.
4. GA
* All QP scenarios continue to reflect very poor recoveries. Investigations are ongoing to determine
a cause for these out of control situations but no explanations have been found.
POC for this is Suzanne Jones, X449 1.

Mellor Engineering Corporation/Science and Technology Corporation February 11, 1998
MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Mr. Steve Mallen, Laboratory Support Division
FROM: Suzanne Jones, QA/QC Chemist, MEC/STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report for week ending -BueLfitbei9-, 199-7
1. GB
* 12 hour QP chart has four points out of control with no assignable cause. Both the QP and in-
house data have been trending on the low side of the target concentration for approximately two
weeks. We have investigated conditions in the lab and found no explanations for this occurrence.
Further investigations will continue. 2 hour and Perimeter QP charts look good.
2. VX
* 12 hour QP chart has five points out of control with no assignable cause. VX data is also trending
on the low side of the target concentration. Again, investigations of the analytical procedures have
occurred and no explanations found. The 2 hour QP chart shows three points out of control with
no assignable cause. It also reflects the many "dirty" samples analyzed during this period.
Analysts attempt to decrease the interference problem by running blanks after extremely trashy
chromatograms and by performing short bake-outs if necessary. Perimeter QP chart looks good.
3. [HD
* 12 hour QP chart has one point out of control with no assignable cause. 2 hour QP chart has one
point out of control with no assignable cause. Perimeter QP chart has five points out of control
with no assignable cause, but overall is showing improved recoveries from the past several weeks.
4. GA
* All QP scenarios continue to reflect very poor recoveries. Investigations are ongoing to determine
a cause for these out of control situations but no explanations have been found.
POC for this is Suzanne Jones, X449 1.

Mellor Engineering Corporation/Science and Technology Corporation February 4, 1998
MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Mr. Steve Mallen, Laboratory Support Division
FROM: Suzanne Jones, QA/QC Chemist, MEC?STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report for week ending February 3, 1998
1. GB
* Overall, data looks good.
2. VX
* 12 hour QP chart shows three points out of control with on assignable cause. 2 hour QP chart
shows seven points out of control with no assignable cause. Perimeter QP chart shows three points
out of control with no assignable cause. The laboratory has been extremely hot for the past 2-3
weeks affecting the performance of our GCs, which I believe is reflected in the erratic VX QP data
generated in that time frame.
3. HD
* 12 hour QP chart shows one point out of control with on assignable cause. 2 hour QP chart shows
four points out of control with no assignable cause. Perimeter QP chart shows only three points out
of control with W assignable cause. A definite improvement from past charts but no explanation
for the increased recoveries can be given.
4. GA
* All scenario QP charts show a trend in reduced recovery which, like VX is probably a reflection of
the excessive heat in the building causing unstable conditions with the GC and producing
inaccurate and inconsistent results in the QP data.
POC for this is Suzanne Jones, X4491.

Mellor Engineering Corporation/Science and Technology Corporation October 6, 1998
MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Lucille Forrest
FROM: Steve Freudenberger, MEC/STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QL Report for week ending August 29, 1998
1. Attached is the latest QC report covering the aspiration dates of 16 September - 29
September 1998. In addition, I have attached the latest data from the 2 Hour and
Perimeter scenarios. We have been experiencing high recoveries for these two methods
for the last few weeks. We have now traced the high recovery problems down to the way
the calibration curves are prepared. It was on October 1, 1998 we changed the way the
calibration curves are prepared and as a result all of the QPs that were in question have
been in control. If you have any questions, please give us a call (435-833-4491).
Steve Freudenberger
MEC/STC Team

Mellor Engineering Corp. / Science and Technology Corp. November 12, 1997
MEMORANDUM FOR RECORD
TO: Chief, Laboratory Support Division
FROM: Steve Freudenberger, Laboratory Manager MEC/STC Team
SUBJECT: Weekly QP Report Comments
1. Rererence Memorandum for Mr: Mike Ford, ATTN: Suzanne Jones.
2. Following are some responses and comments based on your review of the
weekly QP report. The numbers and letters in parenthesis reference the
paragraph of the memorandum to Mike Ford.
a. (2a.) The QP spikes have not been changed. The current spike levels
listed in SOP LAB 32-00-01-09, page 13 (attachment 1). The 75% and
125% of the QP's can easily be calculated based on the current spike
levels.
b. (2b(l)) Typo, database corrected.
c. (2b(2)) Typo, database corrected.
d. (2b(3)) Database did not sort correctly. QP data points charted correctly.
e. (2c(1)) See attached copies of chain of custody t gs (attachpent n
Notice that the station numbers . an e p •,,een
monitoring s responsibility to fill in the station number on the chain of
custody tag. Obviously, this in not being done on a consistent basis.
Thus, we are proposing that the station numbers be pre-printed on the tags
(note, we are currently printing up the tags). Thus, in order for this to
happen, monitoring division needs to provide a QP sampling schedule at
least two weeks in advance. Bruce Gilbert is providing us a list. Please
have Paul Wardle of his representative do the same.
f. (2c(2)) See paragraph e.
g. (2d) See paragraph e.
h. (2e(1)) Integration error is when the integrator did not correctly integrate
D 112191 IIII II I 3DA1 92291 DA008835-1
the peak. Usually integration errors are determined by comparing the size
of the QL and its area to that of the QP. If there appears to be an error in
the integration of the QP based on the QL integration the operator will flag
the QP as an error in integration. With the new software update,
integration errors will be corrected as the QP's are reviewed. Please see
attached examples of integration errors. (Attachment 3)
i. (2e(2)) Please specify the data point in question.
j. (2f) See paragraph e.
k. (2g) We are currently into the seventh day of a thirty day study. We have
made up two solution on GA in IPA and Acetonitrile at the GPL level.
QP's have been spiked using both solutions and are being aspirated in the
field.
1. (2h) Zero recovery does not always indicate that a spiking error has
occurred. If there is an ASSIGNABLE reason for a zero recovery, the QP
will be flagged as having an assignable reason for low recovery. Based
on experience and the procedure for spiking the QP's the spiker does not
believe that the QP in question was the result of a spiking error.
Assignable causes will and are not going to be used in a liberal fasion.
j. (21) Instrument gases are checked at the end of each shift. See attached
check list. Attachment 4.
K (3) I'm not sure what a reasonable percent of QP's that are in control
should be, but in my book 96% is a A. I believe that the percentage should be based
on past data of guidance from PMCD.
POC for this action is Steve Freudenberger, x4491.
Steve Freudenberger
MEC/STC
